disappeared from their usual haunts soon
;iftÂ» r the fatal shots were fired.
No one could be found who witnessed
the deed.
The report of the pistol shots was
heard coming from the end of the K>iiK
wharf, where the picturesque boats of the
fishermen He, by sonu- boys who wore
lounging near. A moment after the
crouching form of a man was seen =link-
Ing sway in the darkness and disappear
ing in the tortuous alleyways at the base
of Telegraph Hill.
Ikying half concealed behind a pile of
boat gear was the body of the murder
er's victim. There was a gaping bullet
wound, scarred with powder burns, al
most.in the center of the forehead, nnd a
portion of the upper lip waa torn away,
marking the track (ft the other bullet
lired by the assassin.
Tightly clutched in the right hand of
the murdered "man was a long, thin, keen
edged dagger, whose blade glistened In the
glint of the lantern, carried by the f< w
who rushed to the end of the wharf to
Investigate the cause of the shooting.
A murder had taken place and the mur
dered man apparently had some knowl
edge that his life whs in clanger Just be
fore the fatal shot was fired. The
ence of the dagger clutched In the life
lingers told plainly that when the
foe was met it was a duel to the deaih.
I'ntll late this morning the police were
divided in opinion as to whether the mur
der was the result of a quarrel or whether
the killed man, knowing an enemy was
waiting to kill him, drew his dagger and
prepared to sell his^ life as dearly as pos
sible.
Life was not extinct when the murdered
man waa first found and word was sent
to the Harbor Hospital, but before the
ambulance was started on the way, it
waa recalled and the morgue wagon sent
for.
The news of the murder =oon spread
around the colony of fishermen, who live
near the wharf, and before the police ar
rived the body was surrounded by grief
stricken relatives of the dead man.
It was a heartrending sight. In the dim
light of the lantern the wailing relatives
of the murderer's victim knelt around the
body, and when the police arrived they
fought for the possession of the' remains.
Mothers with babes in their arm;!, men
frenzied by the death of their friend,
brothers and sisters crazed with grief,
fought back the men who would deprive
them of the body of their loved one.
Sergeant Cook and Officers Donohuo,
MoGowan and Gwin were bustled about
like so many shuttlecocks h-"- tho fre zjed
le, and' it took them nearly an hour
to convey the body of the murdered man
from the wharf. On the arrival of the
Morgrue wagon the howls were renewed.
and the struggle grew intense. The wife
and sisters of Scraffino knelt beside his
dead body beating their breasts in grief.
while the brothers, with hands and faces
covered with the blood that was oozing
out of the wounds of the dead man,
struggled for possession. The rfflcers
pushed them back, and as the receiving
coffin was placed alongside the body it
was kicked out of the wny. Again it
was brought close to the body by Depu
ties Hallett and Smith ami the body hur
riedly thrown into it. but again it was
thrown out by stricken relatives, who
tried to drag the remains to their homo
and nt the .same time fight off the police
and the Coroner's deputies. The peace
officials again tried to drive away the
frenzied friends and relatives of the mur
dered fisherman, anu thin tlmo they were
successful in getting the body into the
box and in the Morgue wagon.
At the home of the murdered man
women were lying on the floor, beating
thfÂ»lr heads against the wall?, wailing and
Fobbing, while the men, exhausted from
their struggles, rested their heads on their
arms and sobbed bitterly.
Scraffino was but 27 years old and ha^
only been married a few weeks. His bride
was a pretty girl whom he brought from
Italy on tho Ist of July. He loved her in
tho "land of olives, and when he had by
dint of hard work become the owner of
his own crab-boat he sent for her.
Some of the friends who were at the
wedding of the young couple say that the
murder was committed by a Jealous rival,
who. mad with love for the young girl,
followed her from her native land but ar
rived after the marriage ceremony had
been performed, and in his wrath wreaked
his vengeance by taking the life of tho
happy husband.
The police, however, who care little for
romance, were hunting last night for a
brother-in-law. Antonio Gulseppi, who
answers the description given of the
crouching figure that waa seen slinking
away from the wharf after the fatal shot
was fired. Guiseppi was absent from his

SHIRKED THEIB, DUTY.
Police Judges Compelled to Deal
With "Drunks'' in a Proper
Manner.
Captain Seymour and the Police Judges
had a meeting yesterday morning that
promised ;it first to be a stormy one, but
finally ended in a proper understanding
for future business.
The "drunks" have hern In the habit
of not bfing taken before a Judge , but
Sergeant Wolf of the City Prison without
authority has been constituting himself
a Judge, and every morning discharging
them or dealing with them as the fancy
struck him.
Oiptain Seymour happened to drop into
the prison Wednesday morning and was
astonished when he saw. his subordinate
holding court over the "drunks." He ask
ed for an explanation and at once gave
orders that the drunk cases should be
assigned to the courts the same as the
other cases. The result was that yes
tterday morning each court had its share
of the "drunks." Hence the meeting.
The Judges agreed to take week about
to be at the prison at 9:30 o'clock each
morning to dispose of the cases, and the
friction was over.
YOUNG MEN'S INSTITUTE.
The Grand Body Will Meet in San
Jose on the 29th Inst.â The
State of the Order.
The next session of the Grand Council
of the Young Men's Institute of Califor
nia will be held In San Jose, commencing
on the 29th of the current month.
The grand officers are at this time pre
paring for the great event, and the mem
bership in the Garden City is arranging
for the proper reception of the delegates
i)ii<l their entertainment during the ses-
Bion.
During the past year the order has lost
two councils and has added two â No. 508
in this city and No. 520 in Redwood City.
The membership at this time is about
the same as it was at the time of the pre
vious .session of the grand body, but there
haa been a marked gain in its finance.
From the several reports that have been
received from the entire jurisdiction it
appears that the prospects for a notable
Increase during the coming year are very
bright.
Land Office Records Destroyed.
The lire at Susanvllle, Lassen County,
I which, acording to the dispatches to The
i Call yesterday, destroyed the larger part
of the town, has thrown the local office
of the United States Surveyor General in
to confusion. Surveyor General Gleaves
yesterday received information that the
fire had destroyed the Land Office of the
unfortunate town and all of the land
records had been consumed in tho blaze.
This will make It necessary for his office
force to furnish certified copies of all the
records and plats and other data relating
to the lands In the northeastern part of
the State. Certified copies of the land en
tries will have to be obtained from Wash
ington. Mr. Gleaves believes that he will
have to increase hia force, and that even
then it will take at least six months to
finish the extra work caused by the de
struction of the Susanville records.

The Fire Department.
The Fire Commissioners met yesterday
afternoon and accepted the resignation of
M. F. Welsh of Engine 2. James Mason,
engineer of Engine 33, was retired on a
pension. Thomas Johnston was appointed
hoseman of Engine 33; William Heaney,
engineer of Engine 33, and John Hennes
sey, hoseman of Engine 2--

MADE THE HIT OF HIS LIFE
Fell During His Act ; Caught in a Chandelier and Bounded on
the Stage, With Smiles and Bows, Amid a Shower
of Broken Glass.
TORA. a little Japanese who performs on the end of a long: pole that Is
balanced on the shoulder of his acrobatic partner, Mizuna. at ths Co
lumbia Music Hall at Eddy and Mason street!;, turned an accident, that
for fi moment looked as though It might be serious. Into a pretty flnalo
of their wonderful balancing feat that brought him fame.
The stage of the music hall was not intended for acrobatic exhibitions
and down the center of It hangs a large and glittering chandelier contain
ing a myriad incandescent lights. The Royal Tokio acrobats, of which
Tora is a member, came to the city without having first secured an en
gagement at any of the regular amusement places where such perform
ances are specialties, and they tqok the first opening that was offered. In
their pole balancing feats the acrobats are obliged to dodge all around the
chandelier.
On Wednesday night little Tora was squirming about on the end of tho
balanced pole, twenty-five feet in the air, apparently enjoying himself and
amazing the audience, when Mizuna, who was balancing the pole on his
shoulder, slipped. The pole began to totter and Mizuna was unable to
save the little fellow on the top of it from a fall. Some ladies in the audi
ence screamed and men shuddered at the impending catastrophe. Tora
felt the pole going from under him but he retained his presence Oi mind,
and with a graceful swing Jumped for the chandelier. It was about fifteen
feet from the floor of the stage. There was a crash as he landed among
the incandescent lights and smashing glass fell in a shower about the head
of Mizuna. Tora was unhurt, but the chandelier was a wreck. The littlo
Jap waved his hand reas.*>>ringly at the audience, then, with a swing, he
bounded from his perch and turning a somersault as he went through the
air, landed smiling and bowing in the middle of the stage. The frightened
Mizuna hugged the lad in his delight at his escape from injury, while the
men cheered and the women wept in their gladness.
ANOTHER NATIVE DAUGHTER CHOSEN
MISS EVA DENNISON of Sacramento, Who Will
ADDear in "Trilbu."
The latest aspirant to histrionic honors from California, which has fur
nished more than its quota of prominent actresses to the stage, is Miss
Eva Dennison of Sacramento. She has been engaged by Manager T. Daniel
Prawley, and will make her first professional appearance in the revival
of "Trilby," to be given at the Columbia next week. Miss Dennison Is the
daughter of Dan Dennison, the well-known horseman of the capital city,
and who was at one time actively engaged In business in San Francisco.
Miss Dennison is young, petite and graceful, and has an attractive person
ality. Furthermore, she is self-possessed, and if she fulfills the promise
of her amateur work will prove an acceptable addition to the list of profes
sionals.
The young lady will appear as Honorine, and her friends expect her
to do justice to their estimation of her abilities.

BAD SCHOOL FACILITIES.
Residents of Noe Valley Indignant
Over the Actions of the
School Board.
Residents of Noe Valley are indignant
over the manner in which the School
Board has provided for the children in
that district. At the last meeting of the
board, prior to adjournment for the an
nual vacation, a committee from tho West
of Castro-street Improvement Club ap
peared and culled attention to the fact
that the present school building is not
large enough by half to accommodate the
children of the district. They also point
ed out a building conveniently located,
which Is large enough to accommodate all
the children turned away from the regu
lar schoolhouae. A promise was made
that this, or some other building, would
;ted to accommodate the overflow.
Instead of keeping to their promise, how
ever, tf 1 >_- members of the board rented
seven small buildings scattered tirough
out the district, each of which was large
â ] to accommodate one cl.ips and the
result is that the children are scattered all
through the district. Jt is also said that
tho sanitary condition of many of the
buildings is very bad and they are alto
gether unfitted for occupation as schools.
